<span id="freeTextContainer8282288048072761690">Night Road by Kristin Hannah is one of those books that just keeps coming up on book club reads. Having now read it I have to say you cannot read Night Road and not be emotionally affected by the story and the characters.<br/><br/>This is a novel which is without doubt a page turner and by the first 50 pages I was totally drawn in by the story and the characters and I was interest and connected to the story.<br/>Being a mother I could certainly identify with the worries a parent has when a child enters teenage</span>
  <span id="freeText8282288048072761690" style="display:none">Night Road by Kristin Hannah is one of those books that just keeps coming up on book club reads. Having now read it I have to say you cannot read Night Road and not be emotionally affected by the story and the characters.<br /><br />This is a novel which is without doubt a page turner and by the first 50 pages I was totally drawn in by the story and the characters and I was interest and connected to the story.<br />Being a mother I could certainly identify with the worries a parent has when a child enters teenage years and the difficulties that comes with parenting. <br /><br />Second half of the novel was a let down for me as I found it quite predictable. I am not a fan of endings tied up in a bow, I prefer book that leave you guessing or at least leave a few loose ends. I love books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8442457.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> as I like characters that are edgy and a plot that packs a punch.<br />Having said that Night Road is one of those books that is very readable and I know many of my friends will love it.<br /></span>

<div id="review_158315387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158315387" />
    <a title="Melissa (LifeFullyBooked)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/721595-melissa-lifefullybooked"><img alt="Melissa (LifeFullyBooked)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559343382p2/721595.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17757666580574850345">I listened to this on audio and once again I have to say that I think that my experience of the book was enhanced because of this. The narrator (Kathleen McInerney) was brilliant, and I never felt like like I was listening to someone reading the story. Although the story has quite a few cliches and at times felt a bit teenagey for me, I felt for all the characters, especially Jude. I didn't understand or agree with all her actions, but then I've never been in her situation. I normally only liste</span>
  <span id="freeText17757666580574850345" style="display:none">I listened to this on audio and once again I have to say that I think that my experience of the book was enhanced because of this. The narrator (Kathleen McInerney) was brilliant, and I never felt like like I was listening to someone reading the story. Although the story has quite a few cliches and at times felt a bit teenagey for me, I felt for all the characters, especially Jude. I didn't understand or agree with all her actions, but then I've never been in her situation. I normally only listen to audio books while driving, but I could not put this down, so even listened to it in my normal reading time. Warning: this book is a tearjerker, so maybe not best for listening to in public. I highly recommend this to anyone who enjoyes Jodi Picoult.<br /></span>

<div id="review_161205947" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161205947" />
    <a title="Nomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes"><img alt="Nomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499148999p2/3842653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161205947?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nomes" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161205947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14176939321926981646">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Night Road has many elements that attracted me:<br/><br/>girl best friends, one girl in love with the others (forbidden) twin brother<br/><br/>a fateful tragic summer evening<br/><br/>idyllic childhoods, promises and broken hearts<br/><br/>the whole leaving childhood behind thing<br/><br/>watching devastating consequences play out...<br/><br/><blockquote> People on the island still talk about what happened in the summer of '04. They sit on bar stools and in porch swings and spout opinions, half-truths, making judgements that aren't theirs to make. They thin</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14176939321926981646" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Night Road has many elements that attracted me:<br /><br />girl best friends, one girl in love with the others (forbidden) twin brother<br /><br />a fateful tragic summer evening<br /><br />idyllic childhoods, promises and broken hearts<br /><br />the whole leaving childhood behind thing<br /><br />watching devastating consequences play out...<br /><br /><blockquote> People on the island still talk about what happened in the summer of '04. They sit on bar stools and in porch swings and spout opinions, half-truths, making judgements that aren't theirs to make. They think a few columns in the newspaper give them the facts they need. But the facts are hardly what matter... (page 2) </blockquote><br /><br />Night Road is commercial fiction, and while literary is my first love, commercial is my guilty pleasure. I often need a book that doesn't require anything of me but to curl up and get carried away into a story. Which is exactly what I did with Night Road. I read it within 24 hours and it was deliciously satisfying.<br /><br />Night Road has perfect cross-over appeal for young adults looking to dabble in adult fiction. As the story opens, Lexi, Mia and Zach are 14 years old and meeting for the first time. By chapter three, they are seniors in high school and for a good chunk of the book they are teenagers. <br /><br />Plot-wise ~ I always enjoy books that follow characters through their lives a little and this one spans from early teens to mid-twenties. There's some foreshadowing so that some of the events that take place are predictable. I enjoy that kind of foreshadowing as it creates tension and expectation. What, however, is not predictable is the way the events will play out (!). Oh my gosh! Kristin Hannah really puts her characters through the wringer...<br /><br />Which is why I managed to get the unputdownable sucked in feeling half way through.<br /><br />I found the book incredibly easy to sink into and once the Main Event occurs (just past a third of the way in) I was completely addicted and utterly engrossed. <br /><br />And that's what defines a guilty pleasure for me: when I know a book doesn't have the greatest literary merit (you know what I'm saying here...) but I am completely sucked into the story anyway. <br /><br />The prose is nothing to get excited about (it is rather effortless and smooth) and at times characters and plot points are a tad cliché. Some of the characters felt a little two-dimensional, but it didn't particularly faze me as it is more a plot-driven than character-driven novel. <br /><br />To go with an analogy, it was like that addictiveness of made-for-tv movies: not as brilliant or block-buster-y as Hollywood A-list movies ~ but completely absorbing and just plain good times (well, despite the tragedy of it all). Also, sheepishly, I even found myself tear-y at one point towards the end (!)<br /><br />As for what I got tear-y about? The story is kind of haunting and sorrowful and devastating and hopeful, full of dreams (that get dashed) and it's also a little bit tender. It stars some really infuriating characters (those ones you love to hate...). It also featured a side plot (nicely done) that always always gets me ~ the neglected little child...aww. <br /><br />I had a good good time reading this and I have already added more of Kristin Hannah's titles to my to-read list. She is similar in style/feel/genre to LESLEY PEARCE and perhaps LESLEY LOKKO (although, IMO, superior to LOKKO). <br /><br />Also, my review ~ whoa, brackets all over the place (haha), I keep interrupting myself in my own review :D <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14176939321926981646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1470880298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1470880298" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5222160-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525911009p2/5222160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1470880298?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/5222160-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1470880298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2340952178830438151">When Lexi Baill moves to Washington to live with her aunt after the death of her mother, she doesn't have any unrealistic dreams of finding acceptance and a loving home. Lexi has lived her life in and out of foster homes based on the ability of her drug addict mother to properly care for her between prison sentences and stints in rehab facilities. On her first day of school in Washington, Lexi meets Mia Farraday, a rich girl who is also a social outcast. Over the next four years, Lexi and Mia ar</span>
  <span id="freeText2340952178830438151" style="display:none">When Lexi Baill moves to Washington to live with her aunt after the death of her mother, she doesn't have any unrealistic dreams of finding acceptance and a loving home. Lexi has lived her life in and out of foster homes based on the ability of her drug addict mother to properly care for her between prison sentences and stints in rehab facilities. On her first day of school in Washington, Lexi meets Mia Farraday, a rich girl who is also a social outcast. Over the next four years, Lexi and Mia are inseparable, but when Lexi starts dating Mia's twin brother Zach, complications arise and one fatal decision will change the lives of all three forever.<br /><br />I absolutely <i>love</i> Kristin Hannah! She knows how to create a story that keeps you interested and wanting to read more. The story is told in alternating perspectives between Lexi and Mia's mother, Jude. The majority of the book I did find myself wanting to hear more of Lexi's view, but the story would not have been nearly the same without an intimate look at Jude's thoughts and feelings.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[After the death of Mia, Jude basically shut down. Nothing had meaning for her anymore. Not her son, not her husband, and most definitely not her grandchild from the girl who <i>murdered</i> her daughter. I wanted to be mad a Jude. For a while, I was definitely extremely irritated with her. But, I've never lost a child. I'm not even a mother. So, I have absolutely no idea how much it would hurt to lose a child that suddenly and that tragically.<br /><br />Vehicular homicide is definitely a difficult situation for all involved. I'm not sure if I agreed with the length of Lexi's sentence. Should there have been some sort of punishment? Absolutely. She made a horrible decision and someone lost their life. But Lexi didn't commit a crime in cold blood, and I felt her sentence was more for setting an example instead of serving justice. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The book did wrap up rather quickly, but I did like and agree with the ending. Definitely a great read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2340952178830438151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2450745067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2450745067" />
    <a title="Jenny Baker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16404316-jenny-baker"><img alt="Jenny Baker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563044810p2/16404316.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2450745067?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny Baker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny Baker" href="/user/show/16404316-jenny-baker">Jenny Baker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16404316-jenny-baker?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16404316-jenny-baker?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2450745067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14066661314484885487">This was a beautiful and heartbreaking story. The audiobook on CD has a fantastic narration!<br/><br/>I was so hooked on this I didn’t want to get out of the car. When I got to work, I sat in the car for ten minutes listening and did the same when I returned home. When I went to the store, I sat in the parking lot for a few minutes to listen. At home, I couldn’t stop thinking about it, so I got the audiobook out of my car and listened to it on my laptop. It’s that good. <br/><br/>There’s so much I want to say, but </span>
  <span id="freeText14066661314484885487" style="display:none">This was a beautiful and heartbreaking story. The audiobook on CD has a fantastic narration!<br /><br />I was so hooked on this I didn’t want to get out of the car. When I got to work, I sat in the car for ten minutes listening and did the same when I returned home. When I went to the store, I sat in the parking lot for a few minutes to listen. At home, I couldn’t stop thinking about it, so I got the audiobook out of my car and listened to it on my laptop. It’s that good. <br /><br />There’s so much I want to say, but they’re spoilers and I want to keep this spoiler free. Sorry if this sounds disjointed and rushed. This is another novel where Kristin Hannah shines. Actually, this is only my second novel of hers, the other being The Great Alone. As a new fan, I’m embarrassed to say that I have yet to read The Nightingale. <br /><br />Her storytelling is spot on and yet again, she does a magnificent job bringing the characters to life. The themes are universal and most of us know someone who experienced something similar. The major turn of events shocked me, although in hindsight, it shouldn’t have. In many ways, it’s so realistic with the underage drinking, struggling to fit in, and the differences in socioeconomic levels between the characters. I felt bitter seeing the privileged family and felt an ache seeing the ones who struggled. I understood some of Lexi’s struggles, mainly growing up poor and feeling like you don’t have any friends. Several times my eyes watered or I gasped as the story unfolded. <br /><br />If you’ve enjoyed some of Kristin Hannah’s other novels, this is a must read for you. Be prepared. This may give you a good cry.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14066661314484885487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer413094663973765833">Enjoyed this! I did take a while for me to get really hooked and not want to put it down. The story was heartbreaking and complicated. My heart aches for all of the characters. I like the way it ended and felt all sorts of emotions throughout. Good read!</span>

<div id="review_255284317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/255284317" />
    <a title="Northwestreader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6488126-northwestreader"><img alt="Northwestreader" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/255284317?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Northwestreader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Northwestreader" href="/user/show/6488126-northwestreader">Northwestreader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255284317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1624760013335801332">This is not a genre that normally appeals to me. I won a set of these books for my book club so I read it. I have children who were in high school more or less at the same time the story took place, we live in Washington where the story is set, and the book jacket makes the story line sound interesting, so I start with the idea that the story will resonate with me.<br/><br/>I did read the whole book, every word of it. This book is akin to an after-school TV special: I could almost hear the music swelling </span>
  <span id="freeText1624760013335801332" style="display:none">This is not a genre that normally appeals to me. I won a set of these books for my book club so I read it. I have children who were in high school more or less at the same time the story took place, we live in Washington where the story is set, and the book jacket makes the story line sound interesting, so I start with the idea that the story will resonate with me.<br /><br />I did read the whole book, every word of it. This book is akin to an after-school TV special: I could almost hear the music swelling as the drama rose.<br /><br />I didn’t care about the characters; they were stereotypical and not very interesting. The plot was full of hyperbole.<br /><br />Next week my book club will discuss this book. I am hoping that the input of my book club friends will push me to raise my opinion of this book. Perhaps we will be able to find a discussion point that leads to some intelligent and thoughtful interchanges. After all, over the years, some of our best discussions have stemmed from some pretty mediocre books.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61405757-jen-brodehl?shelf=childhood-sweethearts">childhood-sweethearts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61405757-jen-brodehl?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61405757-jen-brodehl?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188580673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6869155889696927753">5++ Stars- I was super addicted to this book and couldn’t put it down or stop thinking about it! It had me feeling so many emotions which is what I love about Kristin Hannah. She hooks me in, makes me cry, and gets me to love all of her flawed and authentic characters. I loved Miles and Zach so much!! I did have a hard time with a lot of Lexi’s dumb decisions but I got over it. Love, friendship, loss, hope, forgiveness and healing are big themes in this book. It’s definitely been added to my fav</span>
  <span id="freeText6869155889696927753" style="display:none">5++ Stars- I was super addicted to this book and couldn’t put it down or stop thinking about it! It had me feeling so many emotions which is what I love about Kristin Hannah. She hooks me in, makes me cry, and gets me to love all of her flawed and authentic characters. I loved Miles and Zach so much!! I did have a hard time with a lot of Lexi’s dumb decisions but I got over it. Love, friendship, loss, hope, forgiveness and healing are big themes in this book. It’s definitely been added to my favorites both as a book and as an audiobook (GREAT reader)!</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E4+8dsNWZatgqb0VRMi48b9yRixPqXWHOyxJacsmAQIL6jsJBK2Ik/98eWl0oJEQVQKi40zQpmUxZCQ7TrdiTQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nH++RAFLuWEkkQQvoGxgCZ/Xt4GaB0bk9tItpgubuNOEGjk7xrBUWbtEwFOQBEnodadTTpl+lQb8mkD0jgrbnA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/54493.Kristin_Hannah">About Kristin Hannah</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/54493.Kristin_Hannah"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1517255843p3/54493.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/54493.Kristin_Hannah">Kristin Hannah

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17281152874380017365">Kristin Hannah is the award-winning and bestselling author of more than 20 novels including the international blockbuster, The Nightingale, which was named Goodreads Best Historical fiction novel for 2015 and won the coveted People's Choice award for best fiction in the same year. Additionally, it was named a Best Book of the Year by Amazon, iTunes, Buzzfeed, the Wall Street Journal, Paste, and Th</span>
  <span id="freeText17281152874380017365" style="display:none">Kristin Hannah is the award-winning and bestselling author of more than 20 novels including the international blockbuster, The Nightingale, which was named Goodreads Best Historical fiction novel for 2015 and won the coveted People's Choice award for best fiction in the same year. Additionally, it was named a Best Book of the Year by Amazon, iTunes, Buzzfeed, the Wall Street Journal, Paste, and The Week. Her novel, The Great Alone, was also voted as Goodreads best historical novel of the year in 2018.<br /><br />Kristin's highly anticipated new release, The Four Winds will be published on February 9, 2021 (St. Martin's Press). The novel is a sweeping, emotional story of love, family, and survival, set in Texas and California during the dark days of The Great Depression. It is a portrait of one indomitable woman who will do anything to keep her family together. <br /><br />The Nightingale is currently in production at Tri Star, with award-winning director Melanie Laurent set to direct a cast led by Dakota and Elle Fanning. <br /><br />Firefly Lane, starring Katherine Heigl, Sarah Chalke and Ben Lawson, is set to premiere on Netflix in early 2021.<br /><br /><br /> <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.kristinhannah.com">www.kristinhannah.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17281152874380017365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
